Kennedy was probably assassinated as a result of a <a href="/wiki/Conspiracy_(crime)" class="mw-redirect" title="Conspiracy (crime)">conspiracy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStokes19792_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStokes19792-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> The chief reason for this conclusion was, according to the report's dissent, the subsequently discredited<sup id="cite_ref-CBAReport_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CBAReport-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-JusticeDeptMemo_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JusticeDeptMemo-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> acoustic analysis of a <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_assassination_Dictabelt_recording" title="John F. Kennedy assassination Dictabelt recording">police channel dictabelt recording</a>. The Committee concluded that previous investigations into Oswald's responsibility were "thorough and reliable" but they did not adequately investigate the possibility of a conspiracy, and that Federal agencies performed with "varying degrees of competency".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStokes19792-3_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStokes19792-3-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> Specifically, the FBI and CIA were found to be deficient in sharing information with other agencies and the Warren Commission. Instead of furnishing all information relevant to the investigation, the FBI and CIA only responded to specific requests and were still occasionally inadequate.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStokes1979239-261_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStokes1979239-261-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> Furthermore, the Secret Service did not properly analyze information it possessed prior to the assassination and was inadequately prepared to protect the President.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStokes19792_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStokes19792-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Concerning the conclusions of "probable conspiracy", four of the twelve committee members wrote dissenting opinions.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStokes1979483–511_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStokes1979483–511-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> In accordance with the recommendations of the HSCA, the Dictabelt recording and acoustic evidence of a second assassin was subsequently reexamined. In light of investigative reports from the FBI's Technical Services Division and a specially appointed <a href="/wiki/National_Academy_of_Sciences" title="National Academy of Sciences">National Academy of Sciences</a> Committee determining that "reliable acoustic data do not support a conclusion that there was a second gunman,"<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> the Justice Department concluded "that no persuasive evidence can be identified to support the theory of a conspiracy in ... the assassination of President Kennedy".<sup id="cite_ref-JusticeDeptMemo_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JusticeDeptMemo-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Although the final report and supporting volumes of the HSCA was publicly released, the working papers and primary documents were sealed until 2029 under Congressional rules and only partially released as part of the 1992 JFK Act.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="JFK_Act_and_Assassination_Records_Review_Board">JFK Act and Assassination Records Review Board</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/President_John_F._Kennedy_Assassination_Records_Collection_Act_of_1992" title="President John F. Kennedy Assassination Records Collection Act of 1992">President John F. Kennedy Assassination Records Collection Act of 1992</a></div>
<p>In 1992, the popular but controversial movie <i><a href="/wiki/JFK_(film)" title="JFK (film)">JFK</a></i> had renewed public interest in the assassination and particularly in the still-classified documents referenced in the film's postscript. Largely in response to the film, Congress passed the JFK Act, or "President John F. Kennedy Assassination Records Collection Act of 1992". The goal of the legislation was to collect at the <a href="/wiki/National_Archives_and_Records_Administration" title="National Archives and Records Administration">National Archives</a> and make publicly available all of the assassination-related records held by federal and state government agencies, private citizens and various other organizations.
</p><p>The JFK Act also mandated the creation of an independent office, the <a href="/wiki/Assassination_Records_Review_Board" class="mw-redirect" title="Assassination Records Review Board">Assassination Records Review Board</a>, to review the submitted records for completeness and continued secrecy. The Review Board was not commissioned to make any findings or conclusions regarding the assassination, just to collect and release all related documents. From 1994 until 1998, the Assassination Records Review Board gathered and unsealed about 60,000 documents, consisting of over 4&#160;million pages.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> Government agencies requested that some records remain classified and these were reviewed under section 6 criteria of the JFK Act. There were 29,420 such records and all of them were fully or partially released, with stringent requirements for redaction.
</p><p>A staff report for the Assassinations Records Review Board contended that brain photographs in the Kennedy records are not of Kennedy's brain and show much less damage than Kennedy sustained. Boswell refuted these allegations.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> The Board also found that, conflicting with the photographic images showing no such defect, a number of witnesses, including at both the autopsy and Parkland Hospital, saw a large wound in the back of the president's head.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> The Board and board member, Jeremy Gunn, have also stressed the problems with witness testimony, asking people to weigh all of the evidence, with due concern for human error, rather than take single statements as "proof" for one theory or another.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>All remaining assassination-related records (approximately 5,000 pages) were scheduled to be released by October 26, 2017, with the exception of documents certified for continued postponement by the President under the following conditions:
(1) "continued postponement is made necessary by an identifiable harm to the military, defense, intelligence operations, law enforcement, or conduct of foreign relations" and (2) "the identifiable harm is of such gravity that it outweighs the public interest in disclosure." There is some concern among researchers that significant records, particularly those of the CIA, may still remain classified after 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Trump_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Trump-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> Although these documents may include interesting historical information, all of the records were examined by the Review Board and were not determined to impact the facts of the Kennedy assassination.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBugliosi2007End_Notes_147_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBugliosi2007End_Notes_147-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> President <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a> said in October 2017 that he would not block the release of documents.<sup id="cite_ref-Trump_151-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Trump-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> On 26 April 2018, the deadline set by President Trump to release all JFK records, he blocked the release of some records until October 26, 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Conspiracy_theories">Conspiracy theories</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a href="/wiki/File:JFK_Wooden_Fence.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/JFK_Wooden_Fence.jpg/260px-JFK_Wooden_Fence.jpg" decoding="async" width="260" height="195" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/JFK_Wooden_Fence.jpg/390px-JFK_Wooden_Fence.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/JFK_Wooden_Fence.jpg/520px-JFK_Wooden_Fence.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:JFK_Wooden_Fence.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The wooden fence on the grassy knoll, where many conspiracy theorists believe another gunman stood.</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_assassination_conspiracy_theories" title="John F. Kennedy assassination conspiracy theories">John F. Kennedy assassination conspiracy theories</a></div>
<p>Many conspiracy theories posit that the assassination involved people or organizations in addition to <a href="/wiki/Lee_Harvey_Oswald" title="Lee Harvey Oswald">Lee Harvey Oswald</a>. Most current theories put forth a <a href="/wiki/Criminal_conspiracy" class="mw-redirect" title="Criminal conspiracy">criminal conspiracy</a> involving parties as varied as the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Bureau_of_Investigation" title="Federal Bureau of Investigation">FBI</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Central_Intelligence_Agency" title="Central Intelligence Agency">CIA</a>, the U.S. military,<sup id="cite_ref-ARRB-C1_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ARRB-C1-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Italian-American_Mafia" class="mw-redirect" title="Italian-American Mafia">Mafia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lyndon_B._Johnson" title="Lyndon B. Johnson">Vice President Johnson</a>, <a href="/wiki/President_of_Cuba" title="President of Cuba">Cuban President</a> <a href="/wiki/Fidel_Castro" title="Fidel Castro">Fidel Castro</a>, the <a href="/wiki/KGB" title="KGB">KGB</a>, or some combination of those entities.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Public opinion polls have consistently shown that a majority of Americans believe there was a conspiracy to kill Kennedy. <a href="/wiki/The_Gallup_Organization" class="mw-redirect" title="The Gallup Organization">Gallup</a> polls have also found that only 20–30% of the population believe that Oswald had acted alone. These polls also show that there is no agreement on who else may have been involved.<sup id="cite_ref-Gallup,_Inc_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gallup,_Inc-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Lydia_Saad_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lydia_Saad-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> Former Los Angeles District Attorney <a href="/wiki/Vincent_Bugliosi" title="Vincent Bugliosi">Vincent Bugliosi</a> estimated that a total of 42 groups, 82 assassins, and 214 people had been accused in various Kennedy assassination conspiracy theories.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reactions_to_the_assassination">Reactions to the assassination</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Reactions_to_the_assassination_of_John_F._Kennedy" title="Reactions to the assassination of John F. Kennedy">Reactions to the assassination of John F. Kennedy</a></div>
<p>The assassination evoked stunned reactions worldwide. The first hour after the shooting was a time of great confusion before the President's death was announced. The incident took place during the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>, and it was at first unclear whether the shooting might be part of a larger attack upon the United States. There was also concern whether Vice President Johnson, who had been riding two cars behind in the motorcade, was safe.
</p><p>The news shocked the nation. People wept openly and gathered in department stores to watch the television coverage, while others prayed. Traffic in some areas came to a halt as the news spread from car to car.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> Schools across the United States dismissed their students early.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> Anger against Texas and Texans was reported from some individuals. Various <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Browns" title="Cleveland Browns">Cleveland Browns</a> fans, for example, carried signs at the next Sunday's home game against the <a href="/wiki/Dallas_Cowboys" title="Dallas Cowboys">Dallas Cowboys</a> decrying the city of Dallas as having "killed the President".<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>However, there were also instances of Kennedy's opponents cheering the assassination. A journalist reported rejoicing in the streets of Amarillo, with a woman crying out, “Hey, great, JFK’s croaked!”<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The event left a <a href="/wiki/Flashbulb_memory" title="Flashbulb memory">lasting impression</a> on many worldwide. As with the December 7, 1941 <a href="/wiki/Attack_on_Pearl_Harbor" title="Attack on Pearl Harbor">attack on Pearl Harbor</a> before it and the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">September 11 attacks</a> after it, asking "Where were you when you heard about President Kennedy's assassination" would become a common topic of discussion.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="Artifacts.2C_museums_and_locations_today"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Artifacts,_museums_and_locations_today">Artifacts, museums and locations today</span></h2>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/VC-137C_SAM_26000" title="VC-137C SAM 26000">plane</a> that served as Air Force One at the time of the assassination is on display at the <a href="/wiki/National_Museum_of_the_United_States_Air_Force" title="National Museum of the United States Air Force">National Museum of the United States Air Force</a> in Dayton, Ohio. The <a href="/wiki/SS-100-X" title="SS-100-X">1961 Lincoln Continental limousine</a> is on display at the <a href="/wiki/Henry_Ford_Museum" class="mw-redirect" title="Henry Ford Museum">Henry Ford Museum</a> in Dearborn, Michigan.<sup id="cite_ref-relics_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-relics-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Jacqueline Kennedy's pink suit, the autopsy report, the X-rays, and President Kennedy's blood-stained clothing are in the possession of the National Archives, with access controlled by the Kennedy family. Other items in the Archives include equipment from Parkland Hospital trauma room; Oswald's rifle, diary, and revolver; bullet fragments; and the windshield of Kennedy's limousine.<sup id="cite_ref-relics_169-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-relics-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_Catafalque" title="Lincoln Catafalque">Lincoln Catafalque</a>, on which President Kennedy's coffin rested in the Capitol, is on display at the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Capitol_Visitor_Center" title="United States Capitol Visitor Center">United States Capitol Visitor Center</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1993 the three-acre park within <a href="/wiki/Dealey_Plaza" title="Dealey Plaza">Dealey Plaza</a>, the buildings facing it, the overpass, and a portion of the adjacent railyard&#160;&#8211;&#32;including the railroad switching tower&#160;&#8211;&#32;were incorporated into the Dealey Plaza Historic District by the National Park Service. Much of the area is accessible by visitors, including the park and grassy knoll. Elm Street is still an active thoroughfare; an <i>X</i> painted in the road marks the approximate spot at which the shots struck Kennedy and Connally.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Texas_School_Book_Depository" title="Texas School Book Depository">Texas School Book Depository</a> and its <a href="/wiki/Sixth_Floor_Museum_at_Dealey_Plaza" title="Sixth Floor Museum at Dealey Plaza">Sixth Floor Museum</a> draw over 325,000 visitors annually, and contains a re-creation of the area from which Oswald fired.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> The Sixth Floor Museum also manages the <a href="/wiki/John_Fitzgerald_Kennedy_Memorial" title="John Fitzgerald Kennedy Memorial">John Fitzgerald Kennedy Memorial</a> located one block east of Dealey Plaza.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At the direction of the deceased President's brother, <a href="/wiki/United_States_Attorney_General" title="United States Attorney General">Attorney General</a> <a href="/wiki/Robert_F._Kennedy" title="Robert F. Kennedy">Robert F. Kennedy</a>, some items were destroyed by the United States government. The casket in which President Kennedy's body was transported from Dallas to Washington was dropped into the sea by the Air Force, because "its public display would be extremely offensive and contrary to public policy".<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> Other items, the toe tag on Oswald's corpse, the catalog from which Oswald ordered his clothes worn by Ruby, and a window from the Texas School Book Depository, are in private hands.<sup id="cite_ref-relics_169-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-relics-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup>
The Texas State Archives has the clothes Connally was wearing when he was shot.
The gun Ruby used to kill Oswald later came into the possession of Ruby's brother Earl, and was sold in 1991 for $220,000.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
